To read it, we calculate 31 | | // the length of that partial word and start copying that many 32 | | // bytes into the array. The first word we copy will start with 33 | | // data we don't care about, but the last `lengthmod` bytes will 34 | | // land at the beginning of the contents of the new array. When 35 | | // we're done copying, we overwrite the full first word with 36 | | // the actual length of the slice. 37 | | let lengthmod := and(_length, 31) 38 | | 39 | | // The multiplication in the next line is necessary 40 | | // because when slicing multiples of 32 bytes (lengthmod == 0) 41 | | // the following copy loop was copying the origin's length 42 | | // and then ending prematurely not copying everything it should. 43 | | let mc := add(add(tempBytes, lengthmod), mul(0x20, iszero(lengthmod))) 44 | | let end := add(mc, _length) 45 | | 46 | | for { 47 | | // The multiplication in the next line has the same exact purpose 48 | | // as the one above. 49 | | let cc := add(add(add(_bytes, lengthmod), mul(0x20, iszero(lengthmod))), _start) 50 | | } lt(mc, end) { 51 | | mc := add(mc, 0x20) 52 | | cc := add(cc, 0x20) 53 | | } { 54 | | mstore(mc, mload(cc)) 55 | | } 56 | | 57 | | mstore(tempBytes, _length) 58 | | 59 | | //update free-memory pointer 60 | | //allocating the array padded to 32 bytes like the compiler does now 61 | | mstore(0x40, and(add(mc, 31), not(31))) 62 | | } 63 | | //if we want a zero-length slice let's just return a zero-length array 64 | | default { 65 | | tempBytes := mload(0x40) 66 | | //zero out the 32 bytes slice we are about to return 67 | | //we need to do it because Solidity does not garbage collect 68 | | mstore(tempBytes, 0) 69 | | 70 | | mstore(0x40, add(tempBytes, 0x20)) 71 | | } 72 | | } 73 | | 74 | | return tempBytes; 75 | | } 76 | | 77 | | function toAddress(bytes memory _bytes, uint256 _start) internal pure returns (address) { 78 | | require(_bytes.length >= _start + 20, 'toAddress_outOfBounds'); 79 | | address tempAddress; 80 | | 81 | | assembly { 82 | | tempAddress := div(mload(add(add(_bytes, 0x20), _start)), 0x1000000000000000000000000) 83 | | } 84 | | 85 | | return tempAddress; 86 | | } 87 | | 88 | | function toUint24(bytes memory _bytes, uint256 _start) internal pure returns (uint24) { 89 | | require(_start + 3 >= _start, 'toUint24_overflow'); 90 | | require(_bytes.length >= _start + 3, 'toUint24_outOfBounds'); 91 | | uint24 tempUint; 92 | | 93 | | assembly { 94 | | tempUint := mload(add(add(_bytes, 0x3), _start)) 95 | | } 96 | | 97 | | return tempUint; /home/xshadow/panoptic-v1-core-private/lib/openzeppelin-contracts/contracts/utils/math/Math.sol 1 | | // SPDX-License-Identifier: MIT 2 | | // OpenZeppelin Contracts (last updated v4.8.0) (utils/math/Math.sol) 3 | | 4 | | pragma solidity ^0.8.0; 5 | | 6 | | /** 7 | | * @dev Standard math utilities missing in the Solidity language. 8 | | */ 9 | | library Math { 10 | | enum Rounding { 11 | | Down, // Toward negative infinity 12 | | Up, // Toward infinity 13 | | Zero // Toward zero 14 | | } 15 | | 16 | | /** 17 | | * @dev Returns the largest of two numbers. 18 | | */ 19 | | function max(uint256 a, uint256 b) internal pure returns (uint256) { 20 | | return a > b ? a : b; 21 | | } 22 | | 23 | | /** 24 | | * @dev Returns the smallest of two numbers. 25 | | */ 26 | | function min(uint256 a, uint256 b) internal pure returns (uint256) { 27 | | return a < b ? a : b; 28 | | } 29 | | 30 | | /** 31 | | * @dev Returns the average of two numbers. The result is rounded towards 32 | | * zero. 33 | | */ 34 | | function average(uint256 a, uint256 b) internal pure returns (uint256) { 35 | | // (a + b) / 2 can overflow. 36 | | return (a & b) + (a ^ b) / 2; 37 | | } 38 | | 39 | | /** 40 | | * @dev Returns the ceiling of the division of two numbers. 41 | | * 42 | | * This differs from standard division with `/` in that it rounds up instead 43 | | * of rounding down. 44 | | */ 45 | | function ceilDiv(uint256 a, uint256 b) internal pure returns (uint256) { 46 | | // (a + b - 1) / b can overflow on addition, so we distribute. 47 | | return a == 0 ? 0 : (a - 1) / b + 1; 48 | | } 49 | | 50 | | /** 51 | | * @notice Calculates floor(x * y / denominator) with full precision. Throws if result overflows a uint256 or denominator == 0 52 | | * @dev Original credit to Remco Bloemen under MIT license (https://xn--2-umb.com/21/muldiv) 53 | | * with further edits by Uniswap Labs also under MIT license. 54 | | */ 55 | | function mulDiv( 56 | | uint256 x, 57 | | uint256 y, 58 | | uint256 denominator 59 | | ) internal pure returns (uint256 result) { 60 | | unchecked { 61 | | // 512-bit multiply [prod1 prod0] = x * y. Compute the product mod 2^256 and mod 2^256 - 1, then use 62 | | // use the Chinese Remainder Theorem to reconstruct the 512 bit result. The result is stored in two 256 63 | | // variables such that product = prod1 * 2^256 + prod0. 64 | | uint256 prod0; // Least significant 256 bits of the product 65 | | uint256 prod1; // Most significant 256 bits of the product 66 | | assembly { 67 | | let mm := mulmod(x, y, not(0)) 68 | | prod0 := mul(x, y) 69 | | prod1 := sub(sub(mm, prod0), lt(mm, prod0)) 70 | | } 71 | | 72 | | // Handle non-overflow cases, 256 by 256 division. 73 | | if (prod1 == 0) { 74 | | return prod0 / denominator; 75 | | } 76 | | 77 | | // Make sure the result is less than 2^256. Also prevents denominator == 0. 78 | | require(denominator > prod1); 79 | | 80 | | /////////////////////////////////////////////// 81 | | // 512 by 256 division. 82 | | /////////////////////////////////////////////// 83 | | 84 | | // Make division exact by subtracting the remainder from [prod1 prod0]. 85 | | uint256 remainder; 86 | | assembly { 87 | | // Compute remainder using mulmod. 88 | | remainder := mulmod(x, y, denominator) 89 | | 90 | | // Subtract 256 bit number from 512 bit number. 91 | | prod1 := sub(prod1, gt(remainder, prod0)) 92 | | prod0 := sub(prod0, remainder) 93 | | } 94 | | 95 | | // Factor powers of two out of denominator and compute largest power of two divisor of denominator. Always >= 1. 96 | | // See https://cs.stackexchange.com/q/138556/92363. 97 | | 98 | | // Does not overflow because the denominator cannot be zero at this stage in the function. 99 | | uint256 twos = denominator & (~denominator + 1); 100 | | assembly { 101 | | // Divide denominator by twos. 102 | | denominator := div(denominator, twos) 103 | | 104 | | // Divide [prod1 prod0] by twos. 105 | | prod0 := div(prod0, twos) 106 | | 107 | | // Flip twos such that it is 2^256 / twos. If twos is zero, then it becomes one. 108 | | twos := add(div(sub(0, twos), twos), 1) 109 | | } 110 | | 111 | | // Shift in bits from prod1 into prod0. 112 | | prod0 |= prod1 * twos; 113 | | 114 | | // Invert denominator mod 2^256. Now that denominator is an odd number, it has an inverse modulo 2^256 such 115 | | // that denominator * inv = 1 mod 2^256. Compute the inverse by starting with a seed that is correct for 116 | | // four bits. That is, denominator * inv = 1 mod 2^4. 117 | | uint256 inverse = (3 * denominator) ^ 2; 118 | | 119 | | // Use the Newton-Raphson iteration to improve the precision. Thanks to Hensel's lifting lemma, this also works 120 | | // in modular arithmetic, doubling the correct bits in each step. 121 | | inverse *= 2 - denominator * inverse; // inverse mod 2^8 122 | | inverse *= 2 - denominator * inverse; // inverse mod 2^16 123 | | inverse *= 2 - denominator * inverse; // inverse mod 2^32 124 | | inverse *= 2 - denominator * inverse; // inverse mod 2^64 125 | | inverse *= 2 - denominator * inverse; // inverse mod 2^128 126 | | inverse *= 2 - denominator * inverse; // inverse mod 2^256 127 | | 128 | | // Because the division is now exact we can divide by multiplying with the modular inverse of denominator. 129 | | // This will give us the correct result modulo 2^256. Since the preconditions guarantee that the outcome is 130 | | // less than 2^256, this is the final result. We don't need to compute the high bits of the result and prod1 131 | | // is no longer required. 132 | | result = prod0 * inverse; 133 | | return result; 134 | | } 135 | | } 136 | | 137 | | /** 138 | | * @notice Calculates x * y / denominator with full precision, following the selected rounding direction. 139 | | */ 140 | | function mulDiv( 141 | | uint256 x, 142 | | uint256 y, 143 | | uint256 denominator, 144 | | Rounding rounding 145 | | ) internal pure returns (uint256) { 146 | | uint256 result = mulDiv(x, y, denominator); 147 | | if (rounding == Rounding.Up && mulmod(x, y, denominator) > 0) { 148 | | result += 1; 149 | | } 150 | | return result; 151 | | } 152 | | 153 | | /** 154 | | * @dev Returns the square root of a number. If the number is not a perfect square, the value is rounded down. 155 | | * 156 | | * Inspired by Henry S. Warren, Jr.'s "Hacker's Delight" (Chapter 11). 157 | | */ 158 | | function sqrt(uint256 a) internal pure returns (uint256) { 159 | | if (a == 0) { 160 | | return 0; 161 | | } 162 | | 163 | | // For our first guess, we get the biggest power of 2 which is smaller than the square root of the target. 164 | | // 165 | | // We know that the "msb" (most significant bit) of our target number `a` is a power of 2 such that we have 166 | | // `msb(a) <= a < 2*msb(a)`. This value can be written `msb(a)=2**k` with `k=log2(a)`. 167 | | // 168 | | // This can be rewritten `2**log2(a) <= a < 2**(log2(a) + 1)` 169 | | // → `sqrt(2**k) <= sqrt(a) < sqrt(2**(k+1))` 170 | | // → `2**(k/2) <= sqrt(a) < 2**((k+1)/2) <= 2**(k/2 + 1)` 171 | | // 172 | | // Consequently, `2**(log2(a) / 2)` is a good first approximation of `sqrt(a)` with at least 1 correct bit. 173 | | uint256 result = 1 << (log2(a) >> 1); 174 | | 175 | | // At this point `result` is an estimation with one bit of precision. We know the true value is a uint128, 176 | | // since it is the square root of a uint256. Newton's method converges quadratically (precision doubles at 177 | | // every iteration). We thus need at most 7 iteration to turn our partial result with one bit of precision 178 | | // into the expected uint128 result. 179 | | unchecked { 180 | | result = (result + a / result) >> 1; 181 | | result = (result + a / result) >> 1; 182 | | result = (result + a / result) >> 1; 183 | | result = (result + a / result) >> 1; 184 | | result = (result + a / result) >> 1; 185 | | result = (result + a / result) >> 1; 186 | | result = (result + a / result) >> 1; 187 | | return min(result, a / result); 188 | | } 189 | | } 190 | | 191 | | /** 192 | | * @notice Calculates sqrt(a), following the selected rounding direction. 193 | | */ 194 | | function sqrt(uint256 a, Rounding rounding) internal pure returns (uint256) { 195 | | unchecked { 196 | | uint256 result = sqrt(a); 197 | | return result + (rounding == Rounding.Up && result * result < a ? 1 : 0); 198 | | } 199 | | } 200 | | 201 | | /** 202 | | * @dev Return the log in base 2, rounded down, of a positive value. 203 | | * Returns 0 if given 0. 204 | | */ 205 | | function log2(uint256 value) internal pure returns (uint256) { 206 | | uint256 result = 0; 207 | | unchecked { 208 | | if (value >> 128 > 0) { 209 | | value >>= 128; 210 | | result += 128; 211 | | } 212 | | if (value >> 64 > 0) { 213 | | value >>= 64; 214 | | result += 64; 215 | | } 216 | | if (value >> 32 > 0) { 217 | | value >>= 32; 218 | | result += 32; 219 | | } 220 | | if (value >> 16 > 0) { 221 | | value >>= 16; 222 | | result += 16; 223 | | } 224 | | if (value >> 8 > 0) { 225 | | value >>= 8; 226 | | result += 8; 227 | | } 228 | | if (value >> 4 > 0) { 229 | | value >>= 4; 230 | | result += 4; 231 | | } 232 | | if (value >> 2 > 0) { 233 | | value >>= 2; 234 | | result += 2; 235 | | } 236 | | if (value >> 1 > 0) { 237 | | result += 1; 238 | | } 239 | | } 240 | | return result; 241 | | } 242 | | 243 | | /** 244 | | * @dev Return the log in base 2, following the selected rounding direction, of a positive value. 245 | | * Returns 0 if given 0. 246 | | */ 247 | | function log2(uint256 value, Rounding rounding) internal pure returns (uint256) { 248 | | unchecked { 249 | | uint256 result = log2(value); 250 | | return result + (rounding == Rounding.Up && 1 << result < value ? 1 : 0); 251 | | } 252 | | } 253 | | 254 | | /** 255 | | * @dev Return the log in base 10, rounded down, of a positive value. 256 | | * Returns 0 if given 0. 257 | | */ 258 | | function log10(uint256 value) internal pure returns (uint256) { 259 | | uint256 result = 0; 260 | | unchecked { 261 | | if (value >= 10**64) { 262 | | value /= 10**64; 263 | | result += 64; 264 | | } 265 | | if (value >= 10**32) { 266 | | value /= 10**32; 267 | | result += 32; 268 | | } 269 | | if (value >= 10**16) { 270 | | value /= 10**16; 271 | | result += 16; 272 | | } 273 | | if (value >= 10**8) { 274 | | value /= 10**8; 275 | | result += 8; 276 | | } 277 | | if (value >= 10**4) { 278 | | value /= 10**4; 279 | | result += 4; 280 | | } 281 | | if (value >= 10**2) { 282 | | value /= 10**2; 283 | | result += 2; 284 | | } 285 | | if (value >= 10**1) { 286 | | result += 1; 287 | | } 288 | | } 289 | | return result; 290 | | } 291 | | 292 | | /** 293 | | * @dev Return the log in base 10, following the selected rounding direction, of a positive value. 294 | | * Returns 0 if given 0. 295 | | */ 296 | | function log10(uint256 value, Rounding rounding) internal pure returns (uint256) { 297 | | unchecked { 298 | | uint256 result = log10(value); 299 | | return result + (rounding == Rounding.Up && 10**result < value ? /home/xshadow/panoptic-v1-core-private/lib/solady/src/utils/Base64.sol 1 | | // SPDX-License-Identifier: MIT 2 | | pragma solidity ^0.8.4; 3 | | 4 | | /// @notice Library to encode strings in Base64. 5 | | /// @author Solady (https://github.com/vectorized/solady/blob/main/src/utils/Base64.sol) 6 | | /// @author Modified from Solmate (https://github.com/transmissions11/solmate/blob/main/src/utils/Base64.sol) 7 | | /// @author Modified from (https://github.com/Brechtpd/base64/blob/main/base64.sol) by Brecht Devos - <brecht@loopring.org>. 8 | | library Base64 { 9 | | /// @dev Encodes `data` using the base64 encoding described in RFC 4648. 10 | | /// See: https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc4648 11 | | /// @param fileSafe Whether to replace '+' with '-' and '/' with '_'. 12 | | /// @param noPadding Whether to strip away the padding. 13 | | function encode(bytes memory data, bool fileSafe, bool noPadding) 14 | | internal 15 | | pure 16 | | returns (string memory result) 17 | | { 18 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 19 | | assembly { 20 | | let dataLength := mload(data) 21 | | 22 | | if dataLength { 23 | | // Multiply by 4/3 rounded up. 24 | | // The `shl(2, ...)` is equivalent to multiplying by 4. 25 | | let encodedLength := shl(2, div(add(dataLength, 2), 3)) 26 | | 27 | | // Set `result` to point to the start of the free memory. 28 | | result := mload(0x40) 29 | | 30 | | // Store the table into the scratch space. 31 | | // Offsetted by -1 byte so that the `mload` will load the character. 32 | | // We will rewrite the free memory pointer at `0x40` later with 33 | | // the allocated size. 34 | | // The magic constant 0x0670 will turn "-_" into "+/". 35 | | mstore(0x1f, "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdef") 36 | | mstore(0x3f, xor("ghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789-_", mul(iszero(fileSafe), 0x0670))) 37 | | 38 | | // Skip the first slot, which stores the length. 39 | | let ptr := add(result, 0x20) 40 | | let end := add(ptr, encodedLength) 41 | | 42 | | let dataEnd := add(add(0x20, data), dataLength) 43 | | let dataEndValue := mload(dataEnd) // Cache the value at the `dataEnd` slot. 44 | | mstore(dataEnd, 0x00) // Zeroize the `dataEnd` slot to clear dirty bits. 45 | | 46 | | // Run over the input, 3 bytes at a time. 47 | | for {} 1 {} { 48 | | data := add(data, 3) // Advance 3 bytes. 49 | | let input := mload(data) 50 | | 51 | | // Write 4 bytes. Optimized for fewer stack operations. 52 | | mstore8(0, mload(and(shr(18, input), 0x3F))) 53 | | mstore8(1, mload(and(shr(12, input), 0x3F))) 54 | | mstore8(2, mload(and(shr(6, input), 0x3F))) 55 | | mstore8(3, mload(and(input, 0x3F))) 56 | | mstore(ptr, mload(0x00)) 57 | | 58 | | ptr := add(ptr, 4) // Advance 4 bytes. 59 | | if iszero(lt(ptr, end)) { break } 60 | | } 61 | | mstore(dataEnd, dataEndValue) // Restore the cached value at `dataEnd`. 62 | | mstore(0x40, add(end, 0x20)) // Allocate the memory. 63 | | // Equivalent to `o = [0, 2, 1][dataLength % 3]`. 64 | | let o := div(2, mod(dataLength, 3)) 65 | | // Offset `ptr` and pad with '='. We can simply write over the end. 66 | | mstore(sub(ptr, o), shl(240, 0x3d3d)) 67 | | // Set `o` to zero if there is padding. 68 | | o := mul(iszero(iszero(noPadding)), o) 69 | | mstore(sub(ptr, o), 0) // Zeroize the slot after the string. 70 | | mstore(result, sub(encodedLength, o)) // Store the length. 71 | | } 72 | | } 73 | | } 74 | | 75 | | /// @dev Encodes `data` using the base64 encoding described in RFC 4648. 76 | | /// Equivalent to `encode(data, false, false)`. 77 | | function encode(bytes memory data) internal pure returns (string memory result) { 78 | | result = encode(data, false, false); 79 | | } 80 | | 81 | | /// @dev Encodes `data` using the base64 encoding described in RFC 4648. 82 | | /// Equivalent to `encode(data, fileSafe, false)`. 83 | | function encode(bytes memory data, bool fileSafe) 84 | | internal 85 | | pure 86 | | returns (string memory result) 87 | | { 88 | | result = encode(data, fileSafe, false); 89 | | } 90 | | 91 | | /// @dev Decodes base64 breaks. 99 | | /// 100 | | /// Note: For performance reasons, 101 | | /// this function will NOT revert on invalid `data` inputs. 102 | | /// Outputs for invalid inputs will simply be undefined behaviour. 103 | | /// It is the user's responsibility to ensure that the `data` 104 | | /// is a valid base64 encoded string. 105 | | function decode(string memory data) internal pure returns (bytes the scratch space. 138 | | // Constants are optimized for smaller bytecode with zero gas overhead. 139 | | // `m` also doubles as the mask of the upper 6 bits. 140 | | let m := 0xfc000000fc00686c7074787c8084888c9094989ca0a4a8acb0b4b8bcc0c4c8cc 141 | | mstore(0x5b, m) 142 | | mstore(0x3b, 0x04080c1014181c2024282c3034383c4044484c5054585c6064) 143 | | mstore(0x1a, /*.•°:°.´+˚.*°.˚:*.´•*.+°.•°:´*.´•*.•°.•°:°.´:•˚°.*°.˚:*.´+°.•*/ 34 | | 35 | | /// @dev Returns the base 10 decimal representation of `value`. 36 | | function toString(uint256 value) internal pure returns (string memory str) { 37 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 38 | | assembly { 39 | | // The maximum value of a uint256 contains 78 digits (1 byte per digit), but 40 | | // we allocate 0xa0 bytes to keep the free memory pointer 32-byte word aligned. 41 | | // We will need 1 word for the trailing zeros padding, 1 word for the length, 42 | | // and 3 words for a maximum of 78 digits. 43 | | str := add(mload(0x40), 0x80) 44 | | // Update the free memory pointer to allocate. 45 | | mstore(0x40, add(str, 0x20)) 46 | | // Zeroize the slot after the string. 47 | | mstore(str, 0) 48 | | 49 | | // Cache the end of the memory to calculate the length later. 50 | | let end := str 51 | | 52 | | let w := not(0) // Tsk. 53 | | // We write the string from rightmost digit to leftmost digit. 54 | | // The following is essentially a do-while loop that also handles the zero case. 55 | | for { let temp := value } 1 {} { 56 | | str := add(str, w) // `sub(str, 1)`. 57 | | // Write the character to the pointer. 58 | | // The ASCII index of the '0' character is 48. 59 | | mstore8(str, add(48, mod(temp, 10))) 60 | | // Keep dividing `temp` until zero. 61 | | temp := div(temp, 10) 62 | | if length. 69 | | mstore(str, length) 70 | | } 71 | | } 72 | | 73 | | /// @dev Returns the base 10 decimal representation of `value`. 74 | | function toString(int256 value) internal pure returns (string memory str) { 75 | | if (value >= 0) { 76 | | return toString(uint256(value)); 77 | | } 78 | | unchecked { 79 | | str = toString(~uint256(value) + 1); 80 | | } 81 | | /// @solidity 418 | | /// @dev Returns `subject` all occurrences of `search` replaced with `replacement`. 419 | | function replace(string memory subject, string memory search, string memory replacement) 420 | | internal 421 | | pure 422 | | returns (string memory result) 423 | | { 424 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 425 | | assembly { 426 | | let subjectLength := mload(subject) 427 | | let searchLength := mload(search) 428 | | let replacementLength := mload(replacement) 429 | | 430 | | subject := add(subject, 0x20) 431 | | search := add(search, 0x20) 432 | | replacement := add(replacement, 0x20) 433 | | result := add(mload(0x40), 0x20) 434 | | 435 | | let subjectEnd := add(subject, subjectLength) 436 | | if iszero(gt(searchLength, subjectLength)) { 437 | | let subjectSearchEnd := add(sub(subjectEnd, searchLength), 1) 438 | | let h := 0 439 | | if iszero(lt(searchLength, 0x20)) { h := keccak256(search, searchLength) } 440 | | let m := shl(3, sub(0x20, and(searchLength, 0x1f))) 441 | | let s := mload(search) 442 | | for {} 1 {} { 443 | | let t := mload(subject) 444 | | // Whether the first `searchLength % 32` bytes of 445 | | // `subject` and `search` matches. 446 | | if iszero(shr(m, xor(t, s))) { 447 | | if h { 448 | | if iszero(eq(keccak256(subject, searchLength), h)) { 449 | | mstore(result, t) 450 | | result := add(result, 1) 451 | | subject := add(subject, 1) 452 | | if iszero(lt(subject, subjectSearchEnd)) { break } 453 | | continue 454 | | } 455 | | } 456 | | // Copy the `replacement` one word at a time. 457 | | for { let o := 0 } 1 {} { 458 | | mstore(add(result, o), mload(add(replacement, o))) 459 | | o := add(o, 0x20) 460 | | if iszero(lt(o, replacementLength)) { break } 461 | | } 462 | | result := add(result, replacementLength) 463 | | subject := add(subject, searchLength) 464 | | if searchLength { 465 | | if iszero(lt(subject, subjectSearchEnd)) { break } 466 | | continue 467 | | } 468 | | } 469 | | mstore(result, t) 470 | | result := add(result, 1) 471 | | subject := add(subject, 1) 472 | | if iszero(lt(subject, subjectSearchEnd)) { break } 473 | | } 474 | | } 475 | | 476 | | let resultRemainder := result 477 | | result := add(mload(0x40), 0x20) 478 | | let k := add(sub(resultRemainder, result), sub(subjectEnd, subject)) 479 | | // Copy the rest of the string one word at a time. 480 | | for {} lt(subject, subjectEnd) {} { 481 | | mstore(resultRemainder, mload(subject)) 482 | | resultRemainder := add(resultRemainder, 0x20) 483 | | subject := add(subject, 0x20) 484 | | } 485 | | result := sub(result, 0x20) 486 | | let last := add(add(result, 0x20), k) // Zeroize the slot after the string. 487 | | mstore(last, 0) 488 | | mstore(0x40, add(last, 0x20)) // Allocate the memory. 489 | | mstore(result, k) // Store the length. 490 | | } 491 | | } 492 | | 493 | | /// @dev Returns the byte index of the first location of `search` in `subject`, 494 | | /// searching from left to right, starting from `from`. 495 | | /// Returns `NOT_FOUND` (i.e. `type(uint256).max`) if the `search` is not found. 496 | | function indexOf(string memory subject, string memory search, uint256 from) 497 | | internal 498 | | pure 499 | | returns (uint256 result) 500 | | { 501 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 502 | | assembly { 503 | | for { let subjectLength := mload(subject) } 1 {} { 504 | | if iszero(mload(search)) { 505 | | if iszero(gt(from, subjectLength)) { 506 | | result := from 507 | | break 508 | | } 509 | | result := subjectLength 510 | | break 511 | | } 512 | | let searchLength := mload(search) 513 | | let subjectStart := add(subject, 0x20) 514 | | 515 | | result := not(0) // Initialize to `NOT_FOUND`. 516 | | 517 | | subject := add(subjectStart, from) 518 | | let end := add(sub(add(subjectStart, subjectLength), searchLength), 1) 519 | | 520 | | let m := shl(3, sub(0x20, and(searchLength, 0x1f))) 521 | | let s := mload(add(search, 0x20)) 522 | | 523 | | if iszero(and(lt(subject, end), lt(from, subjectLength))) { break } 524 | | 525 | | if iszero(lt(searchLength, 0x20)) { 526 | | for { let h := keccak256(add(search, 0x20), searchLength) } 1 {} { 527 | | found. 554 | | function indexOf(string memory subject, string memory search) 555 | | internal 556 | | pure 557 | | returns (uint256 result) 558 | | { 559 | | result = indexOf(subject, search, 0); 560 | | } 561 | | 562 | | /// @dev Returns the byte index of the first location of `search` in `subject`, 563 | | /// searching from right to left, starting from `from`. 564 | | /// Returns `NOT_FOUND` (i.e. `type(uint256).max`) if the `search` is not found. 565 | | function lastIndexOf(string memory subject, string memory search, uint256 from) 566 | | internal 567 | | pure 568 | | returns (uint256 result) 569 | | { 570 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 571 | | assembly { 572 | | for {} 1 {} { 573 | | result := not(0) // Initialize to `NOT_FOUND`. 574 | | let searchLength := mload(search) 575 | | if gt(searchLength, mload(subject)) { break } 576 | | let w := result 577 | | 578 | | let fromMax := sub(mload(subject), searchLength) 579 | | if iszero(gt(fromMax, from)) { from := fromMax } 580 | | 581 | | let end := add(add(subject, 0x20), w) 582 | | subject := add(add(subject, 0x20), from) 583 | | if iszero(gt(subject, end)) { break } 584 | | // As this function is not too often used, 585 | | // we shall simply use keccak256 for smaller bytecode size. 586 | | for { let h := keccak256(add(search, 0x20), searchLength) } 1 {} { 587 | | if eq(keccak256(subject, searchLength), h) { 588 | | 1093 | | /// @dev Packs a single string with its length into a single word. 1094 | | /// Returns `bytes32(0)` if the length is zero or greater than 31. 1095 | | function packOne(string memory a) internal pure returns (bytes32 result) { 1096 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 1097 | | assembly { 1098 | | // We don't need to zero right pad the string, 1099 | | // since this is our own custom non-standard packing scheme. 1100 | | result := 1101 | | mul( 1102 | | // Load the length and the bytes. 1103 | | mload(add(a, 0x1f)), 1104 | | // `length != 0 && length < 32`. Abuses underflow. 1105 | | // Assumes that the length is valid and within the block gas limit. 1106 | | lt(sub(mload(a), 1), 0x1f) 1107 | | ) 1108 | | } 1109 | | } 1110 | | 1111 | | /// @dev Unpacks a string packed using {packOne}. 1112 | | /// Returns the empty string if `packed` is `bytes32(0)`. 1113 | | /// If `packed` is not an output of {packOne}, the output behavior is undefined. 1114 | | function unpackOne(bytes32 packed) internal pure returns (string memory result) { 1115 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 1116 | | assembly { 1117 | | // Grab the free memory pointer. 1118 | | result := mload(0x40) 1119 | | // Allocate 2 words (1 for the length, 1 for the bytes). 1120 | | mstore(0x40, add(result, 0x40)) 1121 | | // Zeroize the length slot. 1122 | | mstore(result, 0) 1123 | | // Store the length and bytes. 1124 | | mstore(add(result, 0x1f), packed) 1125 | | // Right pad with zeroes. 1126 | | mstore(add(add(result, 0x20), mload(result)), 0) 1127 | | } 1128 | | } 1129 | | 1130 | | /// @dev Packs two strings with their lengths into a single word. 1131 | | /// Returns `bytes32(0)` if combined length is zero or greater than 30. 1132 | | function packTwo(string memory a, string memory b) internal pure returns (bytes32 result) { 1133 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 1134 | | assembly { 1135 | | let aLength := mload(a) 1136 | | // We don't need to zero right pad the strings, 1137 | | // since this is our own custom non-standard packing scheme. 1138 | | result := 1139 | | mul( 1140 | | // Load the length and the bytes of `a` and `b`. 1141 | | or( 1142 | | shl(shl(3, sub(0x1f, aLength)), mload(add(a, aLength))), 1143 | | mload(sub(add(b, 0x1e), aLength)) 1144 | | ), 1145 | | // `totalLength != 0 && totalLength < 31`. Total 4 words. 1166 | | mstore(0x40, add(resultB, 0x40)) 1167 | | // Zeroize the length slots. 1168 | | mstore(resultA, 0) 1169 | | mstore(resultB, 0) 1170 | | // Store the lengths and bytes. 1171 | | mstore(add(resultA, 0x1f), packed) 1172 | | mstore(add(resultB, 0x1f), mload(add(add(resultA, 0x20), mload(resultA)))) 1173 | | // Right pad with zeroes. 1174 | | mstore(add(add(resultA, 0x20), mload(resultA)), 0) 1175 | | mstore(add(add(resultB, 0x20), mload(resultB)), 0) 1176 | | } 1177 | | } 1178 | | 1179 | | /// @dev Directly returns `a` without copying. 1180 | | function directReturn(string memory a) internal pure { 1181 | | assembly { 1182 | | // Assumes that the string does not start from the scratch space. 1183 | | let retStart := sub(a, 0x20) 1184 | | let retUnpaddedSize := add(mload(a), 0x40) 1185 | | // Right pad with zeroes. /*´:°•.°+.*•´.*:˚.°*.˚•´.°:°•.°•.*•´.*:˚.°*.˚•´.°:°•.°+.*•´.*:*/ 150 | | /* CALLDATA OPERATIONS */ 151 | | /*.•°:°.´+˚.*°.˚:*.´•*.+°.•°:´*.´•*.•°.•°:°.´:•˚°.*°.˚:*.´+°.•*/ 152 | | 153 | | // Calldata compression and decompression using selective run length encoding: 154 | | // - Sequences of 0x00 (up to 128 consecutive). 155 | | // - Sequences of 0xff (up to 32 consecutive). 156 | | // 157 | | // A run length encoded block consists of two bytes: 158 | | // (0) 0x00 159 | | // (1) A control byte with the following bit layout: 160 | | // - [7] `0: 0x00, 1: 0xff`. 161 | | // - [0..6] `runLength - 1`. 162 | | // 163 | | // The first 4 bytes are bitwise negated so that the compressed calldata 164 | | // can be dispatched into the `fallback` and `receive` functions. 165 | | 166 | | /// @dev Returns the compressed `data`. 167 | | function cdCompress(bytes memory data) internal pure returns (bytes memory result) { 168 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 169 | | assembly { 170 | | function rle(v_, o_, d_) -> _o, _d { 171 | | mstore(o_, shl(240, or(and(0xff, add(d_, 0xff)), and(0x80, v_)))) 172 | | _o := add(o_, 2) 173 | | } 174 | | result := mload(0x40) 175 | | let o := add(result, 0x20) 176 | | let z := 0 // Number of consecutive 0x00. 177 | | let y := 0 // Number of consecutive 0xff. 178 | | for { let end := add(data, mload(data)) } iszero(eq(data, end)) {} { 179 | | data := add(data, 1) 180 | | let c := byte(31, mload(data)) 181 | | if iszero(c) { 182 | | if y { o, y := rle(0xff, o, y) } 183 | | z := add(z, 1) 184 | | if eq(z, 0x80) { o, z := rle(0x00, o, 0x80) } 185 | | continue 186 | | } 187 | | if eq(c, 0xff) { 188 | | if z { o, z := rle(0x00, o, z) } 189 | | y := add(y, 1) 190 | | if eq(y, 0x20) { o, y := rle(0xff, o, 0x20) } 191 | | continue 192 | | } 193 | | if y { o, y := rle(0xff, o, y) } 194 | | if z { o, z := rle(0x00, o, z) } 195 | | mstore8(o, c) 196 | | o := add(o, 1) 197 | | } 198 | | if y { o, y := rle(0xff, o, y) } 199 | | if z { o, z := rle(0x00, o, z) } 200 | | // Bitwise negate the first 4 bytes. 201 | | mstore(add(result, 4), not(mload(add(result, 4)))) 202 | | mstore(result, sub(o, add(result, 0x20))) // Store the length. 203 | | mstore(o, 0) // Zeroize the slot after the string. 204 | | mstore(0x40, add(o, 0x20)) // Allocate the memory. 205 | | } 206 | | } 207 | | 208 | | /// @dev Returns the decompressed `data`. 209 | | function cdDecompress(bytes memory data) internal pure returns (bytes memory result) { 210 | | /// @solidity memory-safe-assembly 211 | | assembly { 212 | | if mload(data) { 213 | | result := mload(0x40) 214 | | let o := add(result, 0x20) 215 | | let s := add(data, 4) 216 | | let v := mload(s) 217 | | let end := add(data, mload(data)) 218 | | mstore(s, not(v)) // Bitwise negate the first 4 bytes. 219 | | for {} lt(data, end) {} { 220 | | data := add(data, 1) 221 | | let c := byte(31, mload(data)) 222 | | if iszero(c) { 223 | | data := add(data, 1) 224 | | let d := byte(31, mload(data)) 225 | | // Fill with either 0xff or 0x00. 226 | | mstore(o, not(0)) 227 | | if iszero(gt(d, 0x7f)) { codecopy(o, codesize(), add(d, 1)) } 228 | | o := add(o, add(and(d, 0x7f), 1)) 229 | | continue 230 | | } 231 | | mstore8(o, c) 232 | | o := add(o, 1) 233 | | } 234 | | mstore(s, v) // Restore the first 4 bytes. 235 | | mstore(result, sub(o, add(result, 0x20))) // Store the length. 236 | | mstore(o, 0) // Zeroize the slot after the string. 237 | | mstore(0x40, add(o, 0x20)) // Allocate the memory. 238 | | } 239 | | } 240 | | } 241 | | 242 | | /// @dev To be called in the `fallback` function. 243 | | /// ``` 244 | | /// fallback() external payable { LibZip.cdFallback(); } 245 | | /// receive() external payable {} // Silence compiler warning to add a `receive` function. 246 | | /// ``` 247 | | /// For efficiency, this function will directly return the results, terminating the context. 248 | | /// If called internally, it must be called at the end of the function. 249 | | function cdFallback() internal { 250 | | assembly { 251 | | if iszero(calldatasize()) { return(calldatasize(), calldatasize()) } 252 | | let o := 0 253 | | let f := not(3) // For negating the first 4 bytes. 254 | | for { let i := 0 } lt(i, calldatasize()) {} { 255 | | let c := byte(0, xor(add(i, f), calldataload(i))) 256 | | i := add(i, 1) 257 | | if iszero(c) { 258 | | let d := byte(0, xor(add(i, f), add(and(d, 0x7f), 1)) 264 | | continue 265 | | } 266 | | mstore8(o, c) 267 | | o := add(o, 1) 268 | | } 269 | | let success := delegatecall(gas(), address(), 0x00, o, codesize(), 0x00) 270 | | returndatacopy(0x00, 0x00, returndatasize()) 271 | | if iszero(success) { revert(0x00, returndatasize()) } 272 | | return(0x00, returndatasize()) 273 | | } 274 | | } 275 | | } 276 | |

/home/xshadow/panoptic-v1-core-private/lib/v3-core/contracts/libraries/FullMath.sol 1 | | // SPDX-License-Identifier: MIT 2 | | pragma solidity ^0.8.0; 3 | | 4 | | /// @title Contains 512-bit math functions 5 | | /// @notice Facilitates multiplication and division that can have overflow of an intermediate value without any loss of precision 6 | | /// @dev Handles "phantom overflow" i.e., allows multiplication and division where an intermediate value overflows 256 bits 7 | | library FullMath { 8 | | /// @notice Calculates floor(a×b÷denominator) with full precision. Throws if result overflows a uint256 or denominator == 0 9 | | /// @param a The multiplicand 10 | | /// @param b The multiplier 11 | | /// @param denominator The divisor 12 | | /// @return result The 256-bit result 13 | | /// @dev Credit to Remco Bloemen under MIT license https://xn--2-umb.com/21/muldiv 14 | | function mulDiv( 15 | | uint256 a, 16 | | uint256 b, 17 | | uint256 denominator 18 | | ) internal pure returns (uint256 result) { 19 | | unchecked { 20 | | // 512-bit multiply [prod1 prod0] = a * b 21 | | // Compute the product mod 2**256 and mod 2**256 - 1 22 | | // then use the Chinese Remainder Theorem to reconstruct 23 | | // the 512 bit result. The result is stored in two 256 24 | | // variables such that product = prod1 * 2**256 + prod0 25 | | uint256 prod0; // Least significant 256 bits of the product 26 | | uint256 prod1; // Most significant 256 bits of the product 27 | | assembly { 28 | | let mm := mulmod(a, b, not(0)) 29 | | prod0 := mul(a, b) 30 | | prod1 := sub(sub(mm, prod0), lt(mm, prod0)) 31 | | } 32 | | 33 | | // Handle non-overflow cases, 256 by 256 division 34 | | if (prod1 == 0) { 35 | | require(denominator > 0); 36 | | assembly { 37 | | result := div(prod0, denominator) 38 | | } 39 | | return result; 40 | | } 41 | | 42 | | // Make sure the result is less than 2**256. 43 | | // Also prevents denominator == 0 44 | | require(denominator > prod1); 45 | | 46 | | /////////////////////////////////////////////// 47 | | // 512 by 256 division. 48 | | /////////////////////////////////////////////// 49 | | 50 | | // Make division exact by subtracting the remainder from [prod1 prod0] 51 | | // Compute remainder using mulmod 52 | | uint256 remainder; 53 | | assembly { 54 | | remainder := mulmod(a, b, denominator) 55 | | } 56 | | // Subtract 256 bit number from 512 bit number 57 | | assembly { 58 | | prod1 := sub(prod1, gt(remainder, prod0)) 59 | | prod0 := sub(prod0, remainder) 60 | | } 61 | | 62 | | // Factor powers of two out of denominator 63 | | // Compute largest power of two divisor of denominator. 64 | | // Always >= 1. 65 | | uint256 twos = (0 - denominator) & denominator; 66 | | // Divide denominator by power of two 67 | | assembly { 68 | | denominator := div(denominator, twos) 69 | | } 70 | | 71 | | // Divide [prod1 prod0] by the factors of two 72 | | assembly { 73 | | prod0 := div(prod0, twos) 74 | | } 75 | | // Shift in bits from prod1 into prod0. For this we need 76 | | // to flip `twos` such that it is 2**256 / twos. 77 | | // If twos is zero, then it becomes one 78 | | assembly { 79 | | twos := add(div(sub(0, twos), twos), 1) 80 | | } 81 | | prod0 |= prod1 * twos; 82 | | 83 | | // Invert denominator mod 2**256 84 | | // Now that denominator is an odd number, it has an inverse 85 | | // modulo 2**256 such that denominator * inv = 1 mod 2**256. 86 | | // Compute the inverse by starting with a seed that is correct 87 | | // correct for four bits. That is, denominator * inv = 1 mod 2**4 88 | | uint256 inv = (3 * denominator) ^ 2; 89 | | // Now use Newton-Raphson iteration to improve the precision. 90 | | // Thanks to Hensel's lifting lemma, this also works in modular 91 | | // arithmetic, doubling the correct bits in each step. 92 | | inv *= 2 - denominator * inv; // inverse mod 2**8 93 | | inv *= 2 - denominator * inv; // inverse mod 2**16 94 | | inv *= 2 - denominator * inv; // inverse mod 2**32 95 | | inv *= 2 - denominator * inv; // inverse mod 2**64 96 | | inv *= 2 - denominator * inv; // inverse mod 2**128 97 | | inv *= 2 - denominator * inv; // inverse mod 2**256 98 | | 99 | | // Because the division is now exact we can divide by multiplying 100 | | // with the modular inverse of denominator. This will give us the 101 | | // correct result modulo 2**256. Since the precoditions guarantee 102 | | // that the outcome is less than 2**256, this is the final result. 103 | | // We don't need to compute the high bits of the result and prod1 104 | | // is no longer required. 105 | | result = prod0 * inv; 106 | | return result; 107 | | } 108 | | } 109 | | 110 | | /// @notice Calculates ceil(a×b÷denominator) with full precision. Throws if result overflows a uint256 or denominator == 0 111 | | /// @param a The multiplicand 112 | | /// @param b The multiplier 113 | | /// @param denominator The divisor 114 | | /// @return result The 256-bit result 115 | | function mulDivRoundingUp( 116 | | uint256 a, 117 | | uint256 b, 118 | | uint256 denominator 119 | | ) internal pure returns (uint256 result) { 120 | | unchecked { 121 | | result = mulDiv(a, b, denominator); 122 | | if (mulmod(a, b, denominator) > 0) { 123 | | require(result < type(uint256).max); 124 | | result++; 125 | | } 126 | | } 127 | | } 128 | | } 129 | |

500 | | 501 | | // Short put 502 | | tokenId = addPutLeg(tokenId, start + 1, optionRatio, asset, 0, start, strikeShort, width); 503 | | } 504 | | 505 | | /// @notice creates a diagonal spread with 1 long leg and 1 short leg.abi. 506 | | /// @dev example: createCallDiagonalSpread(uniPoolAddress, 4, 8, -50, 50, 0, 1, 0). 507 | | /// @param univ3pool address of the pool 508 | | /// @param widthLong width of the long leg 509 | | /// @param widthShort width of the short leg 510 | | /// @param strikeLong strike of the long leg 511 | | /// @param strikeShort strike of the short leg 512 | | /// @param asset asset of the spread 513 | | /// @param optionRatio relative size of the spread 514 | | /// @param start leg index where the (2 legs) of the spread begin (usually 0) 515 | | /// @return tokenId the position id with the strategy configured 516 | | function createCallDiagonalSpread( 517 | | address univ3pool, 518 | | int24 widthLong, 519 | | int24 widthShort, 520 | | int24 strikeLong, 521 | | int24 strikeShort, 522 | | uint256 asset, 523 | | uint256 optionRatio, 524 | | uint256 start 525 | | ) public view returns (TokenId tokenId) { 526 | | // Pool 527 | | tokenId = tokenId.addPoolId(SFPM.getPoolId(univ3pool)); 609 | | } 610 | | 611 | | /// @notice creates a calendar spread with 1 long leg and 1 short leg. 612 | | /// @dev example: createCallCalendarSpread(uniPoolAddress, 4, 8, 0, 0, 1, 0). 613 | | /// @param univ3pool address of the pool 614 | | /// @param widthLong width of the long leg 615 | | /// @param widthShort width of the short leg 616 | | /// @param strike strike of the long and short legs 617 | | /// @param asset asset of the spread 618 | | /// @param optionRatio relative size of the spread 619 | | /// @param start leg index where the (2 legs) of the spread begin (usually 0) 620 | | /// @return tokenId the position id with the strategy configured 621 | | function createCallCalendarSpread( 622 | | address univ3pool, 623 | | int24 widthLong, 624 | | int24 widthShort, 625 | | int24 strike, 626 | | uint256 asset, 627 | | uint256 optionRatio, 628 | | uint256 start 629 | | ) public view returns (TokenId tokenId) { 630 | | // calendar spread is a diagonal spread where the legs have identical strike prices 631 | | // so we can create one using the diagonal spread function 632 | | tokenId = createCallDiagonalSpread( 633 | | univ3pool, 634 | | widthLong, 635 | | widthShort, 636 | | strike, 637 | | strike, 638 | | asset, 639 | | optionRatio, 640 | | start 641 | | ); 675 | | } 676 | | 677 | | /// @notice creates iron condor w/ call and put spread. 678 | | /// @dev example: createIronCondor(uniPoolAddress, 4, 50, -50, 50, 0). 679 | | /// @param univ3pool address of the pool 680 | | /// @param width width of the spread 681 | | /// @param callStrike strike of the call spread 682 | | /// @param putStrike strike of the put spread 683 | | /// @param wingWidth width of the wings 684 | | /// @param asset asset of the strategy 685 | | /// @return tokenId the position id with the strategy configured 686 | | function createIronCondor( 687 | | address univ3pool, 688 | | int24 width, 689 | | int24 callStrike, 690 | | int24 putStrike, 691 | | int24 wingWidth, 692 | | uint256 asset 693 | | ) public view returns (TokenId tokenId) { 694 | | // an iron condor is composed of 695 | | // 1. a call spread 696 | | // 2. a put spread 697 | | // the "wings" represent how much more OTM the long sides of the spreads are 698 | | 699 | | // call spread 700 | | tokenId = createCallSpread( 701 | | univ3pool, 702 | | width, 703 | | callStrike + wingWidth, 704 | | callStrike, 705 | | asset, 706 | | 1, 707 | | 0 708 | | );
